## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (nonlinear functions of position x), damping forces (functions of velocity v), and possibly time-dependent driving forces. The system generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - c3 * x**2) * v (Duffing + Van der Pol)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * v (position-dependent stiffness)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (mixed friction model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) ‚Üí symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x**2, x**4) ‚Üí asymmetric potentials indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x**2)*v ‚Üí self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) as in Van der Pol
- Cubic position term with opposite sign to linear term ‚Üí double-well potential (bistability in Duffing systems)
- Sinusoidal or cosinusoidal time dependence ‚Üí external periodic driving force leading to resonance or chaos
- Product of position powers and velocity (x**2 * v) ‚Üí amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of nonlinear dissipation
- Absence of explicit time dependence ‚Üí autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Rational functions of position in restoring force ‚Üí bounded force at large displacements (physical saturation of springs)
- Multiple frequency terms in time ‚Üí quasiperiodic driving leading to complex resonance structures
- Odd functions of velocity in damping ‚Üí energy dissipation that respects time-reversal symmetry breaking consistently
